  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ad407fee-4633-4c95-9c00-0dcdbc6d50aa'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText14385943139406200945" style="display:none">Detective Harry Bosch was sure he'd shot the serial killer responsible for a string of murders in LA . . . but now, a new crime makes him question his convictions.<br /><br />They call him the Dollmaker, a serial killer who stalks Los Angeles and leaves a grisly calling card on the faces of his female victims. When a suspect is shot by Detective Harry Bosch, everyone believes the city's nightmare is over. But then the dead man's widow sues Harry and the LAPD for killing the wrong man--an accusation that rings terrifyingly true when a new corpse is found with the Dollmaker's macabre signature. Now, for the second time, Harry must hunt down a ruthless death-dealer before he strikes again. Careening through a blood-tracked quest, Harry will go from the hard edges of the L.A. night to the last place he ever wanted to go--the darkness of his own heart...</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38455448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17312449724505838827"><br/>I'm not a big fan of novels about serial killers with distinctive M.O.'s who leave clues in notes sent to the lead detective, particularly when the supposed murderer has already been incarcerated or killed, and the possibility of a copycat--or an original injustice--emerges. Been there. Done that. Squared. <br/><br/>But Connelly's novel is so well-plotted and so well-written and features such believable characters and such realistic glimpses into the police detective's world that I was completely won over</span>
  <span id="freeText17312449724505838827" style="display:none"><br />I'm not a big fan of novels about serial killers with distinctive M.O.'s who leave clues in notes sent to the lead detective, particularly when the supposed murderer has already been incarcerated or killed, and the possibility of a copycat--or an original injustice--emerges. Been there. Done that. Squared. <br /><br />But Connelly's novel is so well-plotted and so well-written and features such believable characters and such realistic glimpses into the police detective's world that I was completely won over. Connelly does it right.</span>

<div id="review_95404867" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95404867" />
    <a title="James Thane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane"><img alt="James Thane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442513566p2/3483907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95404867?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Thane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Thane" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane">James Thane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=harry-bosch">harry-bosch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=michael-connelly">michael-connelly</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95404867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5147505682232425511">Four years ago, L. A. homicide detective, Harry Bosch, was part of a task force hunting a sadistic serial killer known as the Dollmaker. The killer preyed on vulnerable women and was blamed for taking the lives of eleven victims. Late one night, after the rest of the team had gone home, Bosch took a frantic call from a prostitute who said that she had just escaped from the Dollmaker. Harry assumed this was probably just another false lead and decided to meet the woman on his way home, without no</span>
  <span id="freeText5147505682232425511" style="display:none">Four years ago, L. A. homicide detective, Harry Bosch, was part of a task force hunting a sadistic serial killer known as the Dollmaker. The killer preyed on vulnerable women and was blamed for taking the lives of eleven victims. Late one night, after the rest of the team had gone home, Bosch took a frantic call from a prostitute who said that she had just escaped from the Dollmaker. Harry assumed this was probably just another false lead and decided to meet the woman on his way home, without notifying anyone else.<br /><br />Upon meeting the victim, though, Bosch concluded that she was credible, especially when she led him back to the small apartment where she said the killer had held her. Through the window, Bosch could see a man moving about in the apartment. He thought about calling for backup, but realized that the Dollmaker might have already lured another victim into the apartment and that he might kill her before reinforcements could arrive. Accordingly, Bosch kicked in the door and found a naked man standing across the floor. Bosch ordered him to freeze, but instead the man reached under a pillow, as if going for a weapon. Bosch fired once, killing the man instantly. Then, lifting up the pillow, he saw that the man had been reaching for a toupee.<br /><br />Once Harry called it in, reinforcements arrived and found solid evidence linking the victim to nine of the eleven killings. The case was declared closed, and in spite of his role in bringing the case to a successful conclusion, Bosch was demoted from the elite Robbery-Homicide Division for failing to call for backup before entering the apartment.<br /><br />Now, four years later, the family of the man Bosch killed is suing him and the department, claiming that Bosch acted recklessly and without cause in shooting the man he believed to be the killer. The trial has barely begun, however, when a new victim is discovered--a blonde who had been killed and encased in concrete. The killing bears all the signature touches of the Dollmaker, but this victim has only been dead for two years. Is it possible after all, that Bosch shot an innocent man?<br /><br />Bosh insists that he did not, and that the new killer must be a copycat. The book thus proceeds along two tracks as Harry stands trial for his actions four years earlier while at the same time hunting a sadistic killer who may or may not have been the real Dollmaker all along. It's a riveting story on both fronts. The courtroom scenes are very well done and will appeal to readers who enjoy legal thrillers. Harry's adversary in court, a female attorney nicknamed "Money" Chandler is a great character in her own right. The hunt for the killer is also edge-of-your-seat stuff, and through it all, Harry is forced to examine the deep, inner darkness of his own soul. All in all, a very solid early entry in a great series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5147505682232425511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1933798810" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1933798810" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1933798810?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=awards">awards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1933798810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9309506830264990458">In book three of the Harry Bosch series, Connelly finally hits his stride. The preceding two books frequently referenced the lethal shooting of a serial killer, a career-changer that resulted in Harry being transferred out of the glamorous (?!) Robbery-Homicide Division and into the hinterlands in Hollywood. In The Concrete Blonde, the case is being tried in a civil court. Harry's refused to plead or settle, and is making do with a lawyer from the D.A.'s office against a top-notch civil rights a</span>
  <span id="freeText9309506830264990458" style="display:none">In book three of the Harry Bosch series, Connelly finally hits his stride. The preceding two books frequently referenced the lethal shooting of a serial killer, a career-changer that resulted in Harry being transferred out of the glamorous (?!) Robbery-Homicide Division and into the hinterlands in Hollywood. In The Concrete Blonde, the case is being tried in a civil court. Harry's refused to plead or settle, and is making do with a lawyer from the D.A.'s office against a top-notch civil rights attorney, Honey Chandler.<br /><br />The tale opens with the very scene where it all began, Bosch and a streetwalker informant watching the apartment of a man who is possibly The Dollmaker, a serial killer who rapes and kills his victims, and then garishly applies makeup to their faces. Segue into the courtroom, where Harry's trial is about to begin. During recess, he gets a call from his lieutenant, asking him to come to a homicide scene. They were led there by a note echoing the handwriting and style of The Dollmaker, and the information in the rhyme has led detectives to a woman buried in concrete. Harry is sure in his gut that he shot the right man, so is this the work of a copycat or is Harry wrong?<br /><br />It's an reasonably intriguing premise--aside from Harry's gut doing the detecting--made urgent by the trial. To add to the tension, it appears someone has leaked information to the prosecuting attorney, so it isn't long before Harry and his somewhat inept attorney are threatened with contempt of court. The back and forth from the courtroom to solving the mystery of the woman in concrete keep the pace moving. His relationship with Sylvia provides a counterpoint to the sordidness of the case and the trial.<br /><br />One of the strange things about the series for me is the 80s setting. It's so odd to think of a time of pagers and public telephones. In-time information isn't quite as much of a lynch pin in this case, so it's easier to ignore. There's a couple of red herrings, the first quite obvious, the second less so, but the law of character conservation holds. I will note that it's a relief for a mystery-thriller to not feel the need to explore the serial-killer POV.<br /><br />Although Connelly still has a rather flat, simplistic writing style, he seems to be improving stylistically, or at least allowing himself to drift away from the narrow confines of Harry's basic world-view. A couple of points was almost poetic, as Harry muses at various points about the nature of justice.<br /><b><br />"The lack of hospitality exists because the federal government does not want its courthouse to give even the appearance that justice may be slow, or nonexistent... There is enough of that going on across Spring Street in the County Criminal Courts building. Every day the benches in the hallways of every floor are clogged with those who wait. Mostly they are women and children, their husbands or fathers or lovers held in lockup. Mostly they are black or brown. Mostly the benches look like crowded life rafts--women and children first--with people pressed together and cast adrift, waiting, always waiting, to be found."<br /></b><br />A game changer for me as well. Fast-paced, I devoured it in one night. I'll definitely be moving on with the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9309506830264990458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3355143239" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3355143239" />
    <a title="Joe Valdez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez"><img alt="Joe Valdez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585885999p2/26876584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3355143239?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe Valdez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe Valdez" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez">Joe Valdez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35215588-the-concrete-blonde">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3355143239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16201140199197850189">As research for a novel I'm writing, I've been reading detective fiction and stealing everything of value. My story takes place in L.A. of the early '90s and burgling Michael Connelly turned out to be a bonanza. Not only has Connelly written 22 Harry Bosch novels--basis for the Amazon series <i>Bosch</i>, which in its sixth season, combines one or more books, updated to present day, per season--but the literary Harry Bosch, LAPD homicide detective, begins in Los Angeles of the early '90s. I jumped over</span>
  <span id="freeText16201140199197850189" style="display:none">As research for a novel I'm writing, I've been reading detective fiction and stealing everything of value. My story takes place in L.A. of the early '90s and burgling Michael Connelly turned out to be a bonanza. Not only has Connelly written 22 Harry Bosch novels--basis for the Amazon series <i>Bosch</i>, which in its sixth season, combines one or more books, updated to present day, per season--but the literary Harry Bosch, LAPD homicide detective, begins in Los Angeles of the early '90s. I jumped over the second Bosch novel <i>The Black Ice</i> for the third, <i>The Concrete Blonde</i>, which is set exclusively in L.A.<br /><br /><b>Publish date:</b> June 1, 1994<br /><br /><b>Story:</b> Detective Harry Bosch is being sued in U.S. District Court by the widow of Norman Church, an aerospace worker who Bosch shot while investigating the Dollmaker serial murders which preceded the first novel. The widow is represented by civil rights attorney Honey Chandler, a feared trial lawyer who looks poised to destroy Bosch's city-appointed defense attorney even before new developments in the Dollmaker case. The police receive a note similar to the ones of the Dollmaker's killing spree which directs them to the ashes of a pool hall on Hollywood and Western, burned to the ground in the L.A. Riots the year previous. <br /><br />Police find a remains of a woman entombed in concrete, strangled and presented in the same manner of the Dollmaker killings, suggesting that Bosch might have shot the wrong man. While his defense is getting pounded in civil court, Bosch begins making inquiries that lead him to discover the victim's identity, an adult film player and prostitute who went missing three years ago. Bosch's work land him a spot in the Robbery-Homicide Division task force which presumes that two of the victims attributed to the Dollmaker were actually the work of a copycat they dub the Follower, whose expertise with the investigation suggests he could be another cop and is still out there.<br /><br /><b>L.A. scenery</b>: Much of the novel takes place in the U.S. District Courthouse in downtown L.A. as Bosch and the LAPD are sued for damages. Bosch still lives up on Mulholland Drive in his small house dangling over the Hollywood Hills. His investigation briefly takes him to the San Fernando Valley to a mob-operated adult videostore, the home of a psychologist on Lookout Mountain Drive in Laurel Canyon and to North Hollywood in a sleazy area where prostitutes can work a day shift.<br /><br /><b>1990s nostalgia:</b> Who remembers VCRs and videostores? Both play key roles in Bosch unraveling the mystery. You see, it used to be when you watched physical media, it was on a reel to reel product encased in plastic called a "videotape." Some people recording video on their phones still refer to what they're doing as "taping," even though there's no tape inside our phones. To identify a murder victim, Bosch can't use the Internet or Pornhub, but has to visit an adult videostore to browse videotape boxes. Most adult videostores were not operated by the mob. Connelly just throws that in here for added tension.<br /><br /><b>Opening paragraph:</b> <i>There are no benches in the hallways of the U.S. District Courthouse in downtown Los Angeles. No place to sit. Anybody who slides down the wall to sit on the cold marble floor will get rousted by the first deputy marshal who walks by. And the marshals are always out in the halls, walking by.</i><br /><br /><b>Title in text:</b> <i>His mind wandered to the statue at the courthouse steps. He still couldn't think of her name. <b>A concrete blonde</b>, Chandler had called her. Bosch wondered what Chandler had thought about justice at the end. At her end. He knew there was no justice without hope. Did she still have any left at the end? He believed that she did. Like the pure blue flame dimming to nothing, it was still there. Still hot. It was what allowed her to beat Bremmer.</i><br /><br /><b>Select prose:</b> <i>Terry Lloyd took the witness stand like a man who was as familiar with it as the recliner chair he got drunk in every night in front of the TV set. He even adjusted the microphone in front of him without any help from the clerk. Lloyd had a drinker's badge of a nose and unusually dark brown hair for a man his age, which was pushing sixty. That was because it was obvious to everyone who looked at him, except maybe himself, that he wore a rug. Chandler went through some preliminary questions, establishing that he was a lieutenant in the LAPD's elite Robbery-Homicide Division.</i><br /><br /><b>Closing paragraph:</b> <i>"I didn't know, Sylvia," he said. "I hoped."</i><br /><br /><b>Thoughts:</b> I've seen every variation on the "stop the psycho" genre but was tremendously impressed by <i>The Concrete Blonde</i>. Good band, better book. I think the Bosch novels are too long, but the detail on civil court proceedings or the RHD make this much more than another "stop the psycho" variation and I appreciated that. Because I'm drawn to whatever female character is in a book, I also loved what Connelly did with Honey Chandler. She could've been written as a bad guy or everything corrupt with the legal system and though Bosch gets his editorial asides in at the expense of the system, he respects Chandler's game. Amid Connelly's voluminous research, there's Bosch and I felt a strong sense of wanting to see him solve the mystery.<br /><br />Word count: 176,702 words</span>
  <a data-text-id="16201140199197850189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6543351144186640628">Four years ago, Harry Bosch shot and killed Norman Church who was believed to be the infamous serial killer, The Dollmaker.   <span id="freeText6543351144186640628" style="display:none">Four years ago, Harry Bosch shot and killed Norman Church who was believed to be the infamous serial killer, The Dollmaker. Now, his widow is suing Harry for wrongful death and his career is on the line. It gets even more complicated when another body is discovered during the trial, supposedly killed by The Dollmaker <i>after</i> Church's death. <br /><br />A significant part of the story covers the trial, which really serves as the anchor for all else going on as Harry and the original task force try to investigate the new murder. My list of primary suspects changed so much I lost count as there were quite a few surprises, twists and red herrings (even Harry gets sidetracked). I'm still crazy about Harry and this is another fine installment in the series. Dick Hill's narration continues to be spot on for Harry and I'm grateful there're so many books ahead of me.</span>

<div id="review_2358971012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358971012" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2358971012?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2358971012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9119937597153766622">Very good.<br/><br/>Crime fiction fans took notice of writer Michael Connelly and his hero detective Hieronymus "Harry" Bosch after the strong first and second books featuring Bosch, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32508.The_Black_Echo__Harry_Bosch___1__Harry_Bosch_Universe___1_' title='The Black Echo (Harry Bosch, #1; Harry Bosch Universe, #1) by Michael Connelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Black Echo</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24244.The_Black_Ice__Harry_Bosch___2__Harry_Bosch_Universe___2_' title='The Black Ice (Harry Bosch, #2; Harry Bosch Universe, #2) by Michael Connelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Black Ice</a>. The two “Black” books were solid, but also had some sophomoric problems that held them back from being truly exceptional.<br/><br/>Connelly’s 1994 Bosch book, and third in the series, shows him writing with confidence and flair – this is a writer hitting his stride and stepping up his game. Not only wa</span>
  <span id="freeText9119937597153766622" style="display:none">Very good.<br><br>Crime fiction fans took notice of writer Michael Connelly and his hero detective Hieronymus "Harry" Bosch after the strong first and second books featuring Bosch, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32508.The_Black_Echo__Harry_Bosch___1__Harry_Bosch_Universe___1_" title="The Black Echo (Harry Bosch, #1; Harry Bosch Universe, #1) by Michael Connelly" rel="nofollow noopener">The Black Echo</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24244.The_Black_Ice__Harry_Bosch___2__Harry_Bosch_Universe___2_" title="The Black Ice (Harry Bosch, #2; Harry Bosch Universe, #2) by Michael Connelly" rel="nofollow noopener">The Black Ice</a>. The two “Black” books were solid, but also had some sophomoric problems that held them back from being truly exceptional.<br><br>Connelly’s 1994 Bosch book, and third in the series, shows him writing with confidence and flair – this is a writer hitting his stride and stepping up his game. Not only was this a riveting page turner and a model for the mystery / thriller genre; this went a long way to demonstrate some candid and accessible characterization and backstory for the charismatic but complicated protagonist. Whereas Black Echo devolved sometimes into kitsch cliché and Black Ice may have been overly ambitious, The Concrete Blonde has a quick pace and a relentless plot. <br><br>Connelly’s writing is like Dave Chappelle’s humor – edgy and uncomfortable, but also with credence and thought provoking. And entertaining as hell. Connelly goes further than to just spin a cool story, he explores themes of justice, civil rights, and the nature of law enforcement as well as the psychology of killers and the police and what motivates both to act.<br><br>Four years earlier, Bosch had shot a suspect when the man chose not to FREEZE! when Harry confronted him. Though the man was tied to several murders, Bosch’ handling of the arrest was criticized and now Harry and the LAPD are facing a civil rights trial with the killer’s widow sitting at the plaintiff’s table next to high priced shark lawyer Honey “Money” Chandler. Chandler, a seasoned and talented litigator, is looking to make a fortune and even casts shadows of doubt on whether her client’s late husband was even the right man. This looks to blow up out of control when a new body is found – murdered AFTER Harry killed the killer.<br><br>Tightly wound, this keeps a frenetic stride though the seedy sex industry of LA as the police try to solve the newly discovered murder while the civil trial is ongoing and then as we wait for a verdict. Most alarming is that it appears the killer may have been an insider. The police procedural aspects of the book and the group dynamic Connelly describes with the investigation team further heightens what is already a great book.<br><br>Not just for Connelly – Bosch fans, this is well written, first rate crime fiction. Highly recommended.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1523760456i/25379420._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="266" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9119937597153766622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780759505469" href="/book/show/2050279.The_Concrete_Blonde">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6755739-mark?shelf=police-stories">police-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6755739-mark?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6755739-mark?shelf=american-writers">american-writers</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3320007893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17638431517492792580">Well her is Harry Bosch again this time he is in court having to to account his actions in killing the supposed killer <i>the Dollmaker</i> the family of the deceased is not convinced that their husband and father was a killer. During the lawsuit it turns out that there was not one but a second killer disguising his kills, and that seems to become a problem for Bosch in this new court-case with Honey Chandler leading the defense of the family who feels that Bosch did the wrong thing.<br/><br/>Another serial kill</span>
  <span id="freeText17638431517492792580" style="display:none">Well her is Harry Bosch again this time he is in court having to to account his actions in killing the supposed killer <i>the Dollmaker</i> the family of the deceased is not convinced that their husband and father was a killer. During the lawsuit it turns out that there was not one but a second killer disguising his kills, and that seems to become a problem for Bosch in this new court-case with Honey Chandler leading the defense of the family who feels that Bosch did the wrong thing.<br /><br />Another serial killer another book, you get tired of the serial killer story, but somehow Connelly managed to make it a very readable story in which you follow Bosch through his lawsuit and chase of the second killer. Connelly does give the story some grounding and also shows that police work Bosch style is grinding away until you get it right.<br />This time Bosch has a lady in his life who does matter and does play a role in life of importance and she also gets caught up in his life. <br />The blonde in title is a death body that starts the suspicion that the original serial killer was not alone and her dead does lead to a correction in assumptions.<br /><br />This book had some stuff being used in the TV series that is called Bosch on Amazon Prime the lawsuit started season 1 with Honey Chandler, but the book is totally different. The more you read the books the less it looks like the TV series. And Mimi Rogers as Honey Chandler is certainly no Blond and is still playing her part in the show by season 6.<br /><br />A great book that is well deserved in its reread. Onward to the next. </span>

<div id="review_473276540" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473276540" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473276540?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_kindle">ebook_kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473276540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer828752318013402619">I am really enjoying this series. I'm only on book three, but I think that the style and no-nonsense aspect of the writing, combined with a main character that is both weirdly in tune with himself and his emotions, while still being the stereotypical closed off, masculine type, it's just working for me right now. I really loved one scene where, after a separation from his girlfriend, he acknowledges to himself that he can feel his brain separating from her, and that the longer she takes to decid</span>
  <span id="freeText828752318013402619" style="display:none">I am really enjoying this series. I'm only on book three, but I think that the style and no-nonsense aspect of the writing, combined with a main character that is both weirdly in tune with himself and his emotions, while still being the stereotypical closed off, masculine type, it's just working for me right now. I really loved one scene where, after a separation from his girlfriend, he acknowledges to himself that he can feel his brain separating from her, and that the longer she takes to decide about them, the more he will think it's for the best - that she is a distraction, she is a weakness, a target. This kind of thing is, sure, maybe a bit of toxic masculinity masquerading as practicality... but I can also see the true practicality of it, considering what had just happened in the story, and his own sort of protection of her, as well as self-protection. This sort of intuitive knowledge about himself is really interesting and I love that Connelly includes it, because it makes Bosch much more real to me than just the hard, detached detective type. I love that Bosch feels deeply, even if he has trouble showing it all the time. <br /><br />Add to that the fact that the story in this book was just damn good, and I'm super happy that I'm finally getting around to this series after having it sit on my shelves (physically and virtual) for far too long. <br /><br />Compared to the first and second books of the series, this one was by far my favorite. The plot was more where I thought that this series would take me, I guess. Not that the plots in the first two books were BAD, that's not the case at all, it's just that it's not what I expected from an LA detective to be involved in. First we had a bank heist story that spanned continents and time all the way back to Vietnam, and then we have a drug-runner type story... and though I enjoyed both books, I'm glad that this book stuck to LA, and was... more focused, I guess. <br /><br />Ehh, I actually don't know if that's what I want to say, because I don't really think that Books 1 &amp; 2 were UNFOCUSED... it's just that I prefer the serial killer investigation and more PERSONAL story of this book to the sort of "outside" stories of the first two. I liked how Harry was tied up in it, from childhood, in a way, through to now. I liked that it felt like he had a real stake in it. The previous books, of course, put his career, reputation, and life on the line, but it never felt PERSONAL like this did. And I think that's what made this book so much more enjoyable for me, even though in the end, I'm giving it the same rating. <br /><br />I really like how much of Harry's history we're finally learning (even though from the show I knew it from the outset, thanks for that, AMAZON. O_O) and I like how nuanced this story was, and how details from the events referenced in the first two books are finally coming out and being told. The trial especially brought that out, because it's quite easy to see how this could be a vigilante cop trying to clean the streets of people that he perceives as being the type who murder women like his mother. <br /><br />Harry isn't a reliable character, and who knows where and how he might go, but right now I love him for it. He is flawed, and he tends to go against protocol and reaches for the vinegar before the honey, but I feel that he does all of it with the best of intentions. It's the little things that make me side with him, and it's ONLY because of the perspective that we get from omnisciently being privy to his thoughts and feelings. Were I an outsider, I don't know that I wouldn't agree with the charges that he used excessive deadly force without cause. But the little things, like valuing families getting closure for their loved ones, even if those loved ones have little value in society, over capital punishment for the one who did such horrendous deeds, is enough for me to know he's one of the good guys. He might be unorthodox, but I would much rather have him out there than not. <br /><br />I thought that I had the whodunnit figured out 3 or 4 different times, and I was... mostly wrong. I had a fleeting thought about getting it right, but dismissed it. And I love that. I hate when it's too predictable. Make me work and wait for it! :D<br /><br />One other thing that I loved loved loved about this book was the subtle humor running through it. I loved the relationships between the members of the task force, and the way that they interacted with the new stick-in-the-mud Team Leader, making fun of him right under his nose, and him being suspicious but not really able to understand just what happened... it just struck me as funny. (Even though it's a little mean-spirited, but given the situation, sometimes one must find levity and laughter where one can.) <br /><br />This scene in particular made me laugh quite hard... It's a scene where Bosch is calling to check in with the Team Leader. <blockquote>"Hello, this is Los Angeles Police Department Assistant Chief Irvin Irving's office, Lieutenant Hans Rollenberger speaking, how can I help you?" <br />Bosch figured Hans Off must be expecting Irving himself to call in and therefore trotted out the full-count official telephone greeting that was in the officer's manual but was roundly ignored by most of the people who answered phones in the department. <br />Bosch hung up without saying anything and redialed so the lieutenant could go through the whole spiel again.</blockquote> LOL<br /><br />I'm really looking forward to the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="828752318013402619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12305694217825446651" style="display:none">I have read mystery thrillers most of my life, but my husband is lukewarm on a lot of detective type books. He enjoys fantasy/ Sci-fi/horror stuff. But, I talked him into reading this one with me as a "buddy" read. <br />The truth is I couldn't remember if I had read this one or not. I had not. <br />I can't add more to the comments and reviews that have already been posted about his novel. It was just plain awesome. A+ all the way!<br />There is a serial killer, a courtroom drama, Harry's personal life and history all pulled together to make on of the best mystery thrillers ever.<br />If you haven't read this one or any other Connelly novels ,( I can't imagine anyone who hasn't), I highly recommend him. I would though try to read them in order if you can. I didn't, and wish now that I had.</span>

<div id="review_711682412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/711682412" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386404-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351707681p2/8386404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/711682412?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/8386404-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781409116882" href="/book/show/7701372-the-concrete-blonde">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711682412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16264706233087075123">9/10<br/><br/>This was the best Bosch story I have read to date. It might even be the best Connelly novel or at least on par with The Fifth Witness. Each Bosch novel has got better and better so far but it will be a hard act to follow after this!<br/><br/>The story has two aspects, the law room aspect and the on-going serial killer aspect. All linked in some way or another and linked together expertly. It's easy to see how Connelly was able to hit his stride straight away with "The Lincoln Lawyer" as the courtroom </span>
  <span id="freeText16264706233087075123" style="display:none">9/10<br /><br />This was the best Bosch story I have read to date. It might even be the best Connelly novel or at least on par with The Fifth Witness. Each Bosch novel has got better and better so far but it will be a hard act to follow after this!<br /><br />The story has two aspects, the law room aspect and the on-going serial killer aspect. All linked in some way or another and linked together expertly. It's easy to see how Connelly was able to hit his stride straight away with "The Lincoln Lawyer" as the courtroom scenes here zip along with ease and add the dreaded "just one more chapter...." syndrome which doesn't bode well late into the night.<br /><br />Bosch as a character is easily able to hold up the story on his own but it is also the added depth of the surrounding cast which add another layer making it all the more engaging. Jerry Edgar is a standout character from the support and there is a nice little sub-plot there too.<br /><br />I won't say anything on the main story line as there is too much to say and so many chances of ruining the plot for someone else. It is very engaging though and well worth the read. Whilst it could essentially be read as a standalone, as with most of these types of series books, it adds that something extra knowing a bit about the characters from the other novels. "RRRRRRRRooooggggggger dream leader!" goes down as a high point laugh out loud moment in the book too which relieved some of the on-going tension. It's great to have a bit of humour in these sorts of plots.<br /><br />Very much looking forward to the next in the series!<br /><br />If you enjoyed this try "Knots &amp; Crosses" by Ian Rankin</span>
  <a data-text-id="16264706233087075123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2565697204" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2565697204" />
    <a title="kartik narayanan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4070035-kartik-narayanan"><img alt="kartik narayanan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521695201p2/4070035.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2563470884996033454">Hallelujah! <br/><br/>After the disaster that is The Black Ice, The Concrete Blonde restores my faith in Bosch.<br/><br/>It is an excellent book with great detective work as well as tons of red herrings that kept me guessing till the end. Woohoo! Season 1 of the TV series borrows some of the plot from this book. But, while what is kept in the TV series is captivating, the stuff that did not make the cut is even better.   <span id="freeText2563470884996033454" style="display:none">Hallelujah! <br /><br />After the disaster that is The Black Ice, The Concrete Blonde restores my faith in Bosch.<br /><br />It is an excellent book with great detective work as well as tons of red herrings that kept me guessing till the end. Woohoo! Season 1 of the TV series borrows some of the plot from this book. But, while what is kept in the TV series is captivating, the stuff that did not make the cut is even better. The rest of the plot is about figuring out who the serial killer actually is. <br /><br />The book also does an excellent job of throwing suspicion on a character which made me fall for it. When I discovered that I was wrong, I was elated since this does not happen often. <br /><br />The Concrete Blonde also has excellent pacing as well as a satisfying ending. So, in conclusion, woohoo!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191144530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1528674530378323284">When I began the Bosch series, mention on the Dollmaker case and its resultant banishment of the detective led me to wonder if we'd get a flashback book that would cover this major case. Connelly did one better, mixing the Dollmaker case with new developments and a qausi-legal thriller. Connelly at his best.<br/><br/>While Bosch is in civil court, dealingy with the fallout of killing the apparent Dollmaker, a new body surfaces and opens the case wide open. How could the killings keep going on 4 years afte</span>
  <span id="freeText1528674530378323284" style="display:none">When I began the Bosch series, mention on the Dollmaker case and its resultant banishment of the detective led me to wonder if we'd get a flashback book that would cover this major case. Connelly did one better, mixing the Dollmaker case with new developments and a qausi-legal thriller. Connelly at his best.<br /><br />While Bosch is in civil court, dealingy with the fallout of killing the apparent Dollmaker, a new body surfaces and opens the case wide open. How could the killings keep going on 4 years after the death of the apparent murderer? Bosch investigates, while also on trial for the apparent serial killer's murdering ways. Connelly layers great Bosch detective work with his legal thriller abilities; drawing flashbacks and Bosch's guilt with an ongoing investigation into similar murders.<br /><br />Taking the reader into the dark side of the adult film industry, the inner thoughts of Harry Bosch, and a list of potential copycat murderers, Connelly creates an excellent story and keeps you on the edge of your seat from beginning to end. This is the Connelly I came to like in his LINCOLN LAWYER series.<br /><br />Kudos Mr. C. Keep 'em coming!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1528674530378323284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3203119260?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=los-angeles">los-angeles</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3203119260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8293567735890021311"><blockquote>"Justice, Detective Bosch, is just a concrete blonde."</blockquote><br/>I actually thought I was going to hate this about 30 pages in, and was actively side-eying my friends who'd rated it highly because I'm not a fan of courtroom dramas. All the chatter about downtown LA and Spring St. had me thinking about jury duty and how I'm likely to be tapped again. All for doing my civic duty, but ugh, the drive--please let me transfer service is all I wish--I'll go to Compton. But I digress. <blockquote>The city offered so much beau</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8293567735890021311" style="display:none"><blockquote>"Justice, Detective Bosch, is just a concrete blonde."</blockquote><br />I actually thought I was going to hate this about 30 pages in, and was actively side-eying my friends who'd rated it highly because I'm not a fan of courtroom dramas. All the chatter about downtown LA and Spring St. had me thinking about jury duty and how I'm likely to be tapped again. All for doing my civic duty, but ugh, the drive--please let me transfer service is all I wish--I'll go to Compton. But I digress. <blockquote>The city offered so much beauty and yet it offered so much danger and hate. It was a city of shaken confidence, living solely on its stores of hope.</blockquote><br />Bosch is facing a civil suit for his actions during the Dollmaker case. The previous two books kept whispering and dropping tasty bits about the case and its fallout. This is the book where we get <i>all</i> the details. And it is totally worth it; not going to spoil, but so good. Anyway, the opposing counsel, Honey Chandler is a no-holds-barred shark and there's blood in the water. <br /><br />Bosch has a fan in this one. Someone who wants to play; don't ignore me or else. <br /><br />I wanted to hug Harry through most of this book. Bosch is facing professional issues, past issues, and personal issues. <blockquote> Bosch had spoken the word love. He knew now that he must make it either ugly or beautiful. </blockquote> He's growing, yet still making some of the same missteps. Will he pull through? Or wash out. <br /><br /><blockquote>Every twenty-five years or so the city had its soul torched by the fires of reality. But then it drove on. Quickly, without looking back. Like a hit-and-run.</blockquote><br />Thanks again to Eve for pushing me towards this series. <i>xoxo</i></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1982196916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18136941476255578625">Reviewed at <a href='https://crossmyheartbookreviews.blogspot.com/2017/04/the-concrete-blonde-review.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cross My Heart Writings and Reviews</a><br/><br/>Four years after killing Norman Church, aka The Dollmaker, Harry Bosch is being sued for wrongful death by the man’s wife. As Harry defends his actions, another victim’s body is recovered and this one was murdered after the death of The Dollmaker killer casting doubt on Harry’s case. Harry knows it’s looking bad for him. Did he make a mistake? Or is there another explanation?<br/><br/><i>The Concrete Blonde</i> is the perfect blend of suspense and police procedural </span>
  <span id="freeText18136941476255578625" style="display:none">Reviewed at <a href="https://crossmyheartbookreviews.blogspot.com/2017/04/the-concrete-blonde-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Cross My Heart Writings and Reviews</a><br /><br />Four years after killing Norman Church, aka The Dollmaker, Harry Bosch is being sued for wrongful death by the man’s wife. As Harry defends his actions, another victim’s body is recovered and this one was murdered after the death of The Dollmaker killer casting doubt on Harry’s case. Harry knows it’s looking bad for him. Did he make a mistake? Or is there another explanation?<br /><br /><i>The Concrete Blonde</i> is the perfect blend of suspense and police procedural with a touch of romance on the side. Part of the story plays out in the courtroom, revealed through testimonies and Harry’s minefield of thoughts as he filters through all the evidence and possible scenarios, both past and present, contemplating what he is missing. A compelling maze of twists and turns, the story is riveting – a true thriller from cover to cover. And while the investigation and case are top-notch, it’s the character development that I loved most. I finished this book feeling a more intimate connection with Harry – a feeling of knowing more about what makes him tick, why he acts and reacts as he does in both personal and professional situations. Hands down, <i>The Concrete Blonde</i> is my favorite of the Harry Bosch series thus far. Intense, emotional, fascinating from beginning to end. A Must Read!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1801721326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4384515861923352041">I thought this was by far the best book in the first three books of the series. Maybe it's just because Harry had the same girlfriend through the whole book and she had been his girlfriend for the year before the book.<br/><br/>The mystery in this book was alluded to in one of the prior books in the series. Since the series seems to be on an annual publication bases that means the idea for this book was rumbling around in the authors mind for a year or more before the book was written. I think that is int</span>
  <span id="freeText4384515861923352041" style="display:none">I thought this was by far the best book in the first three books of the series. Maybe it's just because Harry had the same girlfriend through the whole book and she had been his girlfriend for the year before the book.<br /><br />The mystery in this book was alluded to in one of the prior books in the series. Since the series seems to be on an annual publication bases that means the idea for this book was rumbling around in the authors mind for a year or more before the book was written. I think that is interesting.<br /><br />This is about another serial killer. And of course Harry solves it. He does not follow all the rules. What he does always has a lot of tension and excitement. And he comes out on top. I am reading the initial books in the series back to back to back to back. So far there is no doubt in my mind about moving right on to the next book. Harry has an MO but knowing that doesn't make things boring.<br /><br />I gave the first two books in the series three stars but I'm giving this one four.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2900760413141925892">3 and half stars.<br/>Ok this is only the 2nd Connelly book I've read (the first being "The Poet") but beginning to see a pattern here. Towards the end you are geared up to one suspect being the killer but then bang no wrong guy, it's another and again no wrong guy it's really this guy. Bosch seemed like an ok</span>
  <span id="freeText2900760413141925892" style="display:none">3 and half stars.<br />Ok this is only the 2nd Connelly book I've read (the first being "The Poet") but beginning to see a pattern here. Towards the end you are geared up to one suspect being the killer but then bang no wrong guy, it's another and again no wrong guy it's really this guy. Kind of unsatisfying because in the end there isn't a real analysis of the actual killer. Fast read though if you want to veg out of your own life for a while &amp; be a super sleuth for one night. Bosch seemed like an ok character, all round good cop ex-'Nam vet but somehow naive about his own motives and what drives him. As this is #3 in the Bosch series wonder if more about him is revealed in the earlier books, it just seems he's painted too nice when he obviously has been fighting his own demons for a long time..<br /><br />oh Jeffrey Dahmer is mentioned in the book as having been a photographer before he started his killing spree and as far as I know I think that is not the case. He did photograph his victims but did not work as a photographer. Correct me if I am wrong. </span>

<div id="review_2432351506" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2432351506" />
    <a title="fleurette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4692637-fleurette"><img alt="fleurette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357165343p2/4692637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2432351506?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="fleurette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="fleurette" href="/user/show/4692637-fleurette">fleurette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4692637-fleurette?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4692637-fleurette?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2432351506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11316240749348778442">I'm nearly sure that this is my first book by Michael Connelly and I loved it. I don't know why it took me so long to read one of his books finally but I'm so glad I finally did it. It is a great story, I couldn't stop reading. I probably should have started with the first book in the series but fortunately it doesn't matter for the story.<br/><br/>Harry Bosch is a very complicated character. Knowing him only from this one book, I can't say I know him well but I don't have an impression that he is underde</span>
  <span id="freeText11316240749348778442" style="display:none">I'm nearly sure that this is my first book by Michael Connelly and I loved it. I don't know why it took me so long to read one of his books finally but I'm so glad I finally did it. It is a great story, I couldn't stop reading. I probably should have started with the first book in the series but fortunately it doesn't matter for the story.<br /><br />Harry Bosch is a very complicated character. Knowing him only from this one book, I can't say I know him well but I don't have an impression that he is underdeveloped. I really like the layers that I see and him being a man of many different shades. I like his devotion for Sylvia and the way he thinks about her as his home. And I enjoy the complicated path of his thoughts and feelings. He is a very good and fascinating hero, I would read some other books from Connelly just for Harry Bosch.<br /><br />But if the other books by this author are as good as this one, I won't have to do this only to see the development of the hero. <i>The Concrete Blonde</i> is a very well-written story. It's suspenseful, with enough twists to keep you on the edge all the time and with believable explanation and close-up. Harry Bosch is a part in a court case, he is accused of killing an innocent man instead of a serial killer - the Dollmaker. Bosch was always convinced that he shot the right man but now the new victim of the Dollmaker is discovered and the detective receives a letter, just like the ones the murderer was sending him back in the days. Is Bosch truly guilty? Or if he killed the right monster, who is responsible for the death of the girl found in the concrete floor? <br /><br />The action is fast and catches you from the first pages. And the story becomes better and better with every page. I can't say that the story is someway extremely innovative or genuinely memorable (I'm afraid I won't remember it in a few months) but it's a great read absolutely worth my time. And this is definitely not my last book from Michael Connelly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11316240749348778442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2564581027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2564581027" />
    <a title="S.P. Aruna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58833010-s-p-aruna"><img alt="S.P. Aruna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471747692p2/58833010.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2564581027?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.P. Aruna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.P. Aruna" href="/user/show/58833010-s-p-aruna">S.P. Aruna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58833010-s-p-aruna?shelf=thriller-mystery">thriller-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2564581027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13682192190268699744">In Harry Bosch's third adventure in the series, the detective is standing trial for his actions in killing a serial killer four years earlier. The story takes place in 1994 Los Angeles when the 1991 Rodney King beating by police and the ensuing 1992 riots are still fresh in the city's minds. <br/><br/>I did like this better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32508.The_Black_Echo__Harry_Bosch___1__Harry_Bosch_Universe___1_' title='The Black Echo (Harry Bosch, #1; Harry Bosch Universe, #1) by Michael Connelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Black Echo</a>. The writing has tightened up by this time in the author's career. But what I really enjoyed was the structure of the plot - courtroom scenes (I'm a sucker for cour</span>
  <span id="freeText13682192190268699744" style="display:none">In Harry Bosch's third adventure in the series, the detective is standing trial for his actions in killing a serial killer four years earlier. The story takes place in 1994 Los Angeles when the 1991 Rodney King beating by police and the ensuing 1992 riots are still fresh in the city's minds. <br /><br />I did like this better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32508.The_Black_Echo__Harry_Bosch___1__Harry_Bosch_Universe___1_" title="The Black Echo (Harry Bosch, #1; Harry Bosch Universe, #1) by Michael Connelly" rel="nofollow noopener">The Black Echo</a>. The writing has tightened up by this time in the author's career. But what I really enjoyed was the structure of the plot - courtroom scenes (I'm a sucker for courtroom drama) intermingled with police investigation, an investigation that relates to the trial. Normally you have the crime(s) and then the trial, but in this story the crimes keep on happening.<br /><br />The focus on sexual deviance and serial killings is fascinating, and the author does give us some creepy insights into crimes of this nature. The police procedural aspect is, as in all of Connelly's books, well described.<br /><br />Not so sure about the disclosure of the killer - the choice of the evil-doer I felt was a bit contrived, with the sole intention (it seems) of preventing the reader from guessing, as the person was only a fringe character, never offering the reader a fair chance at figuring it out. But the demand to come up with a twist ending puts a lot of pressure on mystery/crime writers. After all, it has to be somebody, and it can't be too obvious, or reader interest wanes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13682192190268699744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2395778336" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2395778336" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1394928-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405367803p2/1394928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2395778336?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1394928-laura">Laura</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=crime-thriller-suspense">crime-thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=audio-avail-ill">audio-avail-ill</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=ill-request">ill-request</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=on-laptop">on-laptop</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=on-ipad2">on-ipad2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=library-request">library-request</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2395778336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4404088771250258420">4.25 stars. This series just keeps getting better. I can't say enough about Michael Connelly's work. If you're like me and you enjoy a good crime novel, but could do without lots of violence, language and sex, you should give him a try. Not to say they are free of these things, because they aren't and can be gritty at times, but violence and gore don't predominate his work. <br/><br/>His writing is smart and suspenseful. His background as a journalist on the crime beat permeates his work. You can tell he'</span>
  <span id="freeText4404088771250258420" style="display:none">4.25 stars. This series just keeps getting better. I can't say enough about Michael Connelly's work. If you're like me and you enjoy a good crime novel, but could do without lots of violence, language and sex, you should give him a try. Not to say they are free of these things, because they aren't and can be gritty at times, but violence and gore don't predominate his work. <br /><br />His writing is smart and suspenseful. His background as a journalist on the crime beat permeates his work. You can tell he's spent time in a courtroom, for example, and knows his way around one. Reading this series will give you a good idea what it's like to be a Los Angeles police detective, the good, bad and ugly. <br /><br />His storylines suck you in fast and it's always hard to put his books down. They're interesting, with many unexpected surprises along the way. In this volume, we start to really learn about Bosch's childhood, which adds more layers to an already complex personality. If I had a copy of the next book, I'd dive right into it, because I've become really interested in learning more about him, and how his childhood is affecting his personal life. <br /><br />So many unexpected twists in this one, and it came together so nicely in the end. Connelly always delivers. If you're looking for a page turner, it's hard to go wrong with any of his novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4404088771250258420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23883998?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooke" href="/user/show/126262-brooke">Brooke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316153836" href="/book/show/1430068.The_Concrete_Blonde">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126262-brooke?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126262-brooke?shelf=2008">2008</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23883998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17412021125249863672">In Harry Bosch's third outing, we finally get to learn more about the infamous case that resulted in Bosch's demotion to the Hollywood homicide unit. The Concrete Blonde is more of a legal thriller than a police procedural as the plot revolves around the widow of the serial killer shot by Bosch suing the LAPD. A wrench is thrown into Bosch's defense when more corpses matching the serial killer's MO pop up. <br/><br/>I enjoyed this book more than the first two in the series, although it still hasn't inched</span>
  <span id="freeText17412021125249863672" style="display:none">In Harry Bosch's third outing, we finally get to learn more about the infamous case that resulted in Bosch's demotion to the Hollywood homicide unit. The Concrete Blonde is more of a legal thriller than a police procedural as the plot revolves around the widow of the serial killer shot by Bosch suing the LAPD. A wrench is thrown into Bosch's defense when more corpses matching the serial killer's MO pop up. <br /><br />I enjoyed this book more than the first two in the series, although it still hasn't inched up into 4-star territory for me. There just seems to be a wall between me and Bosch, preventing me from really getting absorbed. Connelly's dialogue is even more natural this time, and the melodrama is at an all-time low, which gives me hope that the series will continue to get better. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3452877570" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3452877570" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8104446-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453203748p2/8104446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3452877570?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/8104446-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3452877570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12182164666782576931">My husband spent 32 years of his life on two different police forces in 2 states and he seldom likes the way the police are portrayed in novels and movies by authors and screenwriters that seem to be wanting to sell the books and theater seats and not paying attention to how they are portraying the men and women that put their lives on the line for the public everyday...but he has always appreciated how Michael Connelly tells their story through the sometimes scarred character of Detective Harry</span>
  <span id="freeText12182164666782576931" style="display:none">My husband spent 32 years of his life on two different police forces in 2 states and he seldom likes the way the police are portrayed in novels and movies by authors and screenwriters that seem to be wanting to sell the books and theater seats and not paying attention to how they are portraying the men and women that put their lives on the line for the public everyday...but he has always appreciated how Michael Connelly tells their story through the sometimes scarred character of Detective Harry Bosch. This novel was one of...if not the best of the series. It was very well researched...and showed how the police not only worked together to solve a heinous crime..but their deep relationships with one another. The courtroom parts were a little off...but I guess that added to the story and certainly gave us a character to hate. The author threw in a lot of twists and there were a lot of suspects that could have been the killer known as the "Follower". I'm surprised none of these books have been made into a movie. Thank you Mr. Connelly for showing how thin that "Thin Blue Line" is that is composed of the men and women that wear the badge every day. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12182164666782576931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
